<div class="hatnote" role="note">This is a <a href="/wiki/Korean_name" title="Korean name">Korean name</a>; the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Korean_family_names" title="List of Korean family names">family name</a> is <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ki_(Korean_name)" title="Ki (Korean name)">Ki</a></i>.</div>
<p><b>Ki Sung-yueng</b> (<a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>: <span lang="ko">ê¸°ì±ì©</span>, <small>Korean pronunciation:Â </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Korean" title="Help:IPA for Korean">[ki sÊ°ÊÅjoÅ]</a></span>; born 24 January 1989) is a <a href="/wiki/South_Korean" title="South Korean">South Korean</a> professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who currently plays as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre_midfielder" title="Centre midfielder">central midfielder</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>, and serves as captain of the <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korean national team</a>.</p>
<p>Ki is known for his vision, technique, long-range passing and shooting, along with his good set-pieces.</p>
<p>He has been a full international for South Korea since 2007, gaining over 70 caps. Ki was selected in their squads for two World Cups and the <a href="/wiki/2011_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2011 AFC Asian Cup">2011</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2015 AFC Asian Cup">2015 AFC Asian Cups</a>, finishing as runner-up in the latter tournament. He has also played at two Olympic Games with his country, winning bronze in <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics â Men's tournament">2012</a>.</p>
<p>On 20 May 2015, Ki was voted as <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> Player of the Year as he netted 8 goals in 33 appearances.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2001, Ki went to <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> to study at <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_College_(Brisbane)" title="John Paul College (Brisbane)">John Paul College</a> under the BSP (Brain Soccer Program) overseen by <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Hopkins" title="Jeff Hopkins">Jeff Hopkins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> His father saw the move as an opportunity for Ki to play football and learn English at the same time. Ki played his youth football for the school team and was part of the team that won the 2004 Bill Turner Cup, the national inter-school U-15 soccer competition. Ki received offers in 2005 from <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">Korean</a> club <a href="/wiki/FC_Seoul" title="FC Seoul">FC Seoul</a> and also <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a> club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brisbane_Roar" title="Brisbane Roar">Brisbane Roar</a> (then Queensland Roar), but decided to move back to <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> to continue his career. After moving back to Korea, Ki attended Kumho high school and then enrolled in Kyonggi University. Since then, Ki has been a fluent English speaker. He went by his English name David in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Ki has also expressed a desire to one day return to Australia to finish his career and raise his family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FC_Seoul">FC Seoul</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: FC Seoul">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ki returned to Korea and joined <a href="/wiki/FC_Seoul" title="FC Seoul">FC Seoul</a> where he played alongside national teammate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lee_Chung-Yong" title="Lee Chung-Yong">Lee Chung-Yong</a>. He was a <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">Substitute</a> in the last match of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Korean_League_Cup" title="2006 Korean League Cup">2006 League Cup</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> but could not play. Under <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Eenol_G%C3%BCne%C5%9F" title="Åenol GÃ¼neÅ">Åenol GÃ¼neÅ</a>, he made his senior debut in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kibio_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-kibio-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2008 season, Ki reinforced his position as a key player of FC Seoul. On 29 October, Ki scored the winning goal against Seoul's biggest rival <a href="/wiki/Suwon_Samsung_Bluewings" title="Suwon Samsung Bluewings">Suwon Samsung Bluewings</a> in 92nd minute. Ki performed a "Kangaroo Ceremony", which he claims to be an imitation of <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Adebayor" title="Emmanuel Adebayor">Emmanuel Adebayor</a>'s ceremony, but <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Bleu" title="Grand Bleu">Suwon fans</a> have argued that this was imitation of 'chicken', which is what many Seoul fans call Suwon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kibio_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-kibio-8">[8]</a></sup> He led the team to an unprecedented <a href="/wiki/K_League" title="K League">K League</a> runners-up position with 4 goals and 1 assist in 21 appearances.</p>
<p>In FC Seoul's first K League match of the 2009 season, Ki scored one goal in the 6â1 drubbing of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chunnam_Dragons" title="Chunnam Dragons">Chunnam Dragons</a>. There was increasing speculation regarding a big move abroad with suitors including <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamburg_SV" title="Hamburg SV">Hamburg SV</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.C._Porto" title="F.C. Porto">Porto</a> among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kibio_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-kibio-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celtic">Celtic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Celtic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 25 August 2009, it was revealed that contact between <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Seoul" title="FC Seoul">FC Seoul</a> had occurred regarding the possibility of Ki's transfer to the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Park" title="Celtic Park">Parkhead</a> club. However, the player's agent stated that an immediate move would be unlikely given FC Seoul's success in the league and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Champions_League" title="Asian Champions League">Asian Champions League</a>. Three days later, Celtic clinched a Â£2.1m transfer for Ki.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kibio_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-kibio-8">[8]</a></sup> He linked up with the Parkhead side in the January transfer window at the end of the K-League season. The signing was confirmed on 13 December 2009 after Ki passed a medical and secured a <a href="/wiki/Work_permit" title="Work permit">work permit</a>. Ki reportedly turned down an offer from English club <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> then of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>. He took the number 18 with "Ki" on his shirt. He made his debut for Celtic in a 1â1 draw against <a href="/wiki/Falkirk_F.C." title="Falkirk F.C.">Falkirk</a> at Celtic Park on 16 January 2010, winning the <i>Man of the Match</i> award from the official Celtic website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KiCeltic2_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-KiCeltic2-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celt1_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-celt1-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> He played a further four games for Celtic that season, but struggled to make much impact in what was a period of upheaval for the club.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1914" data-file-width="1611" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg/220px-Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg/330px-Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg/440px-Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ki_Sung-Yueng_-_celtic.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ki Sung-Yueng playing for Celtic in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ki barely played for Celtic in the first month of season 2010â11, but came off the bench to score his first competitive goal for Celtic on 22 August 2010 with a shot from 25 yards in a 4â0 victory against <a href="/wiki/St_Mirren_F.C." title="St Mirren F.C.">St Mirren</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish Premier League</a> (SPL).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> By the end of October he had become a first team regular and was voted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League_monthly_awards" title="Scottish Premier League monthly awards">SPL Young Player of the Month</a> for October 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YoungOct2010_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-YoungOct2010-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> However, on 30 October 2010, Ki found himself the recipient of apparent racist abuse during a league match away at <a href="/wiki/St_Johnstone_F.C." title="St Johnstone F.C.">St Johnstone</a>. A section of the St Johnstone support were heard making barking noises â 'woofing' â at Ki as he took a corner kick. Chants of "Who ate all the dogs?" were also heard from the home fans throughout the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ki scored his second goal of the season in a 2â2 draw with <a href="/wiki/Inverness_Caledonian_Thistle_F.C." title="Inverness Caledonian Thistle F.C.">Inverness Thistle</a> at Celtic Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> On 26 December 2010, Ki scored against St Johnstone in a 2â0 victory in the SPL,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> in what was his last game for Celtic before travelling to <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> to play for South Korea in the <a href="/wiki/2011_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2011 AFC Asian Cup">2011 AFC Asian Cup</a> during January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> On coming back to Scotland in February, Ki returned to the Celtic first team for the 2â2 draw against <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a> in a Scottish Cup tie at Ibrox. Celtic played a significant part of the game with only ten men after <a href="/wiki/Fraser_Forster" title="Fraser Forster">Fraser Forster</a> was sent off, but the midfield including Ki won praise for the manner in which they dominated the game in the second half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Ki also played in the replay at Celtic Park, an ill-tempered match which Celtic won 1â0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> On 21 May 2011, Ki scored the first goal of Celtic's <a href="/wiki/2011_Scottish_Cup_Final" title="2011 Scottish Cup Final">Scottish Cup Final</a> win against <a href="/wiki/Motherwell_F.C." title="Motherwell F.C.">Motherwell</a> with a left-footed strike from around 35 yards. He also won the official Man of the Match award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sc2011_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-sc2011-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ki started the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Celtic_F.C._season" title="2011â12 Celtic F.C. season">2011â12 campaign</a> in Celtic's opening game against <a href="/wiki/Hibernian_F.C." title="Hibernian F.C.">Hibernian</a> in the SPL. Scoring the second goal in a 2â0 victory, a 25-yard left foot strike into the right hand bottom corner and also won the <i>Man of the Match</i> award from the official Celtic website. He impressed Celtic manager <a href="/wiki/Neil_Lennon" title="Neil Lennon">Neil Lennon</a> so much in the Hibernian game that he said:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">â</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">He's a very important player to us. I rate him very highly. He can go on to be anything he wants to be. We think he is a class player and we're glad he's here. Ki has been very consistent over the past 18 months. He's developing nicely into a class player. He had good presence and good composure on the ball. He has a goal or two in him and his passing range is excellent."</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">â</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Ki then went on to score another goal on 13 August 2011 in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish Premier League</a> in a 5â1 win over <a href="/wiki/Dundee_United_F.C." title="Dundee United F.C.">Dundee United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Park" title="Celtic Park">Celtic Park</a>, a strike into the top left hand corner from the edge of the box.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> A couple of days later it was reported that <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> sides <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> and several clubs from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Premier_League" title="Russian Premier League">Russian Premier League</a> were interested in signing Ki. <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> the next day issued a hands off warning to the interested clubs, saying that it would take a bid of significant proportions for <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> to allow the increasingly important midfielder to leave the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> On 10 September 2011, Ki put <a href="/wiki/Motherwell_F.C." title="Motherwell F.C.">Motherwell</a> to the sword yet again, this time in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish Premier League</a> with a superb strike from outside the box with his right foot. <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> went on to win the game 4â0. On 29 September, he started in Celtic's 1â1 draw with Italian side <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a>, scoring on a penalty after 3 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On 18 December 2011, he scored the second goal of the game as <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> beat <a href="/wiki/St_Johnstone_F.C." title="St Johnstone F.C.">St Johnstone</a> 2â0 at <a href="/wiki/McDiarmid_Park" title="McDiarmid Park">McDiarmid Park</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish Premier League</a>. Over the course of the 2011â2012 campaign, Ki scored 7 goals and had 6 assists, playing a key role in helping Celtic win the Scottish title.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Swansea_City">Swansea City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Swansea City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 24 August 2012, Ki transferred to <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> for around Â£6 million on a three-year deal, which was Swansea's record transfer fee until it was broken by <a href="/wiki/Wilfried_Bony" title="Wilfried Bony">Wilfried Bony</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> He made his debut for the Swans in a 3â1 victory against Barnsley in the second round of the League Cup at Liberty Stadium on 28 August 2012. Wearing a No. 24 jersey, Ki started as a central midfielder and was substituted 76 minutes into the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ki enjoyed a promising debut season in the Premier League. Although he failed to replicate the scoring form he displayed at Celtic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> his passing style drew praise from supporters and critics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and he finished the season with 38 appearances in all competitions. On 24 February 2013, Swansea City competed in the final of the League Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup13_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-cup13-34">[34]</a></sup> Ki played for over an hour in the final in an unfamiliar central defensive role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup13_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-cup13-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup13a_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-cup13a-35">[35]</a></sup> The tactical switch proved to be a success, as Swansea ran out comfortable 5â0 winners against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bradford_City" title="Bradford City">Bradford City</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup13_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-cup13-34">[34]</a></sup> as Ki won his first trophy with the Welsh club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup13a_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-cup13a-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Loan_to_Sunderland">Loan to Sunderland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Loan to Sunderland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1406" data-file-width="860" height="327" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg/200px-Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg/300px-Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg/400px-Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ki_Sung-yueng_v_Cardiff_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ki in action for Sunderland in December 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 31 August 2013, Ki joined <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> on a season-long loan with a mid-season re-call option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> He scored his first goal for Sunderland on 17 December 2013 in a 2â1 League Cup quarter-final win over <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, cutting inside <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Cole" title="Ashley Cole">Ashley Cole</a> then beating goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Mark_Schwarzer" title="Mark Schwarzer">Mark Schwarzer</a> with a low shot in the 119th minute for the winning goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> On 26 December, he scored his second for Sunderland in a 1â0 away win over <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>. Everton goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Tim_Howard" title="Tim Howard">Tim Howard</a> played a short pass to <a href="/wiki/Leon_Osman" title="Leon Osman">Leon Osman</a> who was robbed of the ball by Ki. Howard brought Ki down and was sent off, and Ki converted the <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a> himself to give the Black Cats a vital win. It was Ki's first league goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Ki's third goal for Sunderland came in a 4â1 away win at Fulham, from a well worked set piece by <a href="/wiki/Adam_Johnson_(footballer)" title="Adam Johnson (footballer)">Adam Johnson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 January 2014, Ki reached his second consecutive League Cup Final, albeit with a different club, as he helped Sunderland defeat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_United" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a> 2â1 on penalty kicks after the two-legged semi-final had finished level on aggregate; Ki and <a href="/wiki/Marcos_Alonso_Mendoza" title="Marcos Alonso Mendoza">Marcos Alonso</a> scoring Sunderland's penalties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Ki played for Sunderland against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_City" title="Manchester City">Manchester City</a> in the League Cup Final on 2 March 2014, but despite leading 1â0 at half-time they were overpowered by City in the second half, eventually losing 3â1 to the Manchester side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup14_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-cup14-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sunderland spent most of the Premier League season in the relegation zone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1314rv_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-1314rv-44">[44]</a></sup> but Ki played his part in their recovery, even playing on despite suffering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tendonitis" title="Tendonitis">tendonitis</a> in his knee for several months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clm_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-clm-45">[45]</a></sup> He played his last game for Sunderland on 10 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clm_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-clm-45">[45]</a></sup> Sunderland succeeded in avoiding relegation, and eventually finished 14th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1314rv_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-1314rv-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Swansea">Return to Swansea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Return to Swansea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ki returned to Swansea for the start of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014â15 Premier League">2014â15 Premier League</a> season, stating "This is my third season in the Premier League, and I want to grow as a player and improve to help the team."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> He scored the first goal of the season in a 2â1 win over <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> on 16 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> On 28 August, he signed a new contract to last until 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Ki became a regular in the side under new manager <a href="/wiki/Garry_Monk" title="Garry Monk">Garry Monk</a> and by the end of December had started in every Premier League fixture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Ki didn't play for Swansea during January 2015 as he was away on international duty with South Korea at the Asian Cup. On his return in February, he went straight back in to the side and scored the equalising goal in a 1â1 draw with Sunderland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Swansea lost their next match 2â0 against West Brom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sway_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-sway-51">[51]</a></sup> but ten days recorded their second win of the season over Manchester United, Ki scoring their equalising goal in a 2â1 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In 2016 May 8, he scored against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United F.C.</a> and received good evaluation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On the international stage, Ki has played in the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2007 U-20 World Cup</a> and for the <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korea national team</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_under-23_football_team" title="South Korea national under-23 football team">South Korea U-23 team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korean_international_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Korean_international-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 June 2008, he made his international debut in a <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(AFC)" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification (AFC)">2010 World Cup qualification</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Jordan_national_football_team" title="Jordan national football team">Jordan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korean_international_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Korean_international-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 June 2010 Ki was picked in the 23-man South Korea World Cup squad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> On 12 June Ki played in South Korea's first game of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_World_Cup_soccer" title="2010 World Cup soccer">2010 World Cup</a> against Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WC2010_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-WC2010-56">[56]</a></sup> Ki played a part in all 3 group games and assisted twice in 2 different matches against Greece and Nigeria which helped him and his country get through to the knock-out stages of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WC2010_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-WC2010-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 December 2011, Ki (along with <a href="/wiki/Ji_So-yun" title="Ji So-yun">Ji So-yun</a> of Kobe INAC Japan) was awarded the South Korean Player of the Year award. The decision was announced by the Korean Football Association (KFA) based on his international and club performance in the Scottish Premier League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_2012_Olympics" title="London 2012 Olympics">London 2012 Olympics</a>, he scored the fifth and vital penalty for South Korea in their quarter-final match against Great Britain, allowing South Korea to progress to the semi-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> South Korea lost 3â0 to <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> in the semi-final,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> but defeated <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a> 2â0 in the third-place play-off to win the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medal" title="Olympic medal">Bronze medal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bronze_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-bronze-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ki was selected for the South Korea squad for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> He played in all three games as Korea were eliminated at the group stage after one draw and two defeats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Following the World Cup, Ki was made captain of the national team by new coach Uli Stielike.</p>
<p>Ki also played for South Korea in the <a href="/wiki/2015_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2015 AFC Asian Cup">2015 Asian Cup</a> during January, helping his country reach the final against host nation <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australia_national_football_team" title="Australia national football team">Australia</a>. He provided the assist for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Son_Heung-Min" title="Son Heung-Min">Son Heung-Min</a> to tie the final at 1â1 and force extra time, but the Australians scored again during the extra 30 minutes to win 2â1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asia2015_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-asia2015-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ki confirmed in March 2013 that he was dating actress <a href="/wiki/Han_Hye-jin" title="Han Hye-jin">Han Hye-jin</a>, and announced their engagement in May 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The couple filed their marriage registration on June 25, 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> and wed on July 1 at the Intercontinental Hotel Seoul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Both are devout <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> They have a daughter, born on September 13, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 19 November 2007, Ki wrote "If you are frustrated, why don't you go out and play?" on his <a href="/wiki/Cyworld" title="Cyworld">Cyworld</a> page in response to the criticism by Korean fans after <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_under-23_football_team" title="South Korea national under-23 football team">the South Korea U-23 team</a>'s goalless draw against Uzbekistan.Ki deleted his statement after being heavily condemned for his careless behaviour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 January 2011, during the <a href="/wiki/2011_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2011 AFC Asian Cup">2011 AFC Asian Cup</a> semi-final match between Japan and South Korea, Ki scored the opening goal through a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Ki created a controversy by celebrating his goal by making a monkey face and scratching his cheek in front of a pitch-side camera in an allegedly racist slur at <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup_chief_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-cup_chief-77">[77]</a></sup> Ki initially defended his goal celebration through a Twitter post claiming that he was annoyed at having seen a <a href="/wiki/Rising_Sun_Flag" title="Rising Sun Flag">Rising Sun Flag</a> in the stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spl_racism_claim_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-spl_racism_claim-78">[78]</a></sup> Ki then claimed that the celebration was a reference to alleged racist abuse he had received during <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish Premier League</a> games from opposition fans, but the chief executive of <a href="/wiki/Show_Racism_the_Red_Card" title="Show Racism the Red Card">Show Racism the Red Card</a> expressed scepticism about this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spl_racism_claim_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-spl_racism_claim-78">[78]</a></sup> Asian Cup tournament director Tokuaki Suzuki said that no action will be taken on part of the AFC and that FIFA has not contacted the AFC regarding the matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup_chief_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-cup_chief-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the summer of 2013, it was widely reported that Ki had previously insulted then South Korea national team manager <a href="/wiki/Choi_Kang-hee_(footballer)" title="Choi Kang-hee (footballer)">Choi Kang-hee</a> on his Facebook page before and after the match against Kuwait in February 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Ki wrote, "Now everyone should have realised the value of the players who play overseas. [He] should have left us alone, otherwise, [he] will be hurt."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Ki later apologised for his "mischievous and inappropriate remarks" and his father visited the KFA to apologise as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_goals">International goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ki_Sung-yueng&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: International goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<tr>
<td>1.</td>
